           <dd><em>eta&#x015b;as</em> <em>&#x0101;s</em> m. a Br&#x0101;hman <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#U&#x1e47;">U&#x1e47;.</a></dd>

           <dt>etad </dt>
           <dd><em>et&#x00e1;d</em> mfn. (Gr. 223 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; g. <em>sarv&#x00e2;di</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#P&#x0101;&#x1e47;">P&#x0101;&#x1e47;.</a> 1-1, 27) this, this here, here (especially as pointing to what is nearest to the speaker, e.g. <em>e&#x1e63;a b&#x0101;&#x1e47;a&#x1e25;</em>, this arrow here in my hand </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>e&#x1e63;a y&#x0101;ti panth&#x0101;&#x1e25;</em>, here passes the way </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>e&#x1e63;a k&#x0101;la&#x1e25;</em>, here i.e. now, is the time </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>etad</em>, this here, i.e. this world here below) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes used to give emphasis to the personal pronouns (e.g. <em>e&#x1e63;o'ham</em>, I, this very person here) or with omission of those pronouns (e.g. <em>e&#x1e63;a tv&#x0101;&#x1e43; svarga&#x1e43; nay&#x0101;mi</em>, I standing here will convey thee to heaven </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>etau pravi&#x1e63;&#x1e6d;au sva&#x1e25;</em>, we two here have entered) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; as the subject of a sentence it agrees in gender and number with the predicate without reference to the noun to be supplied (e.g. <em>etad eva hi me dhanam</em>, for this <em>scil. cow</em> is my only wealth <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a>) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; but sometimes the neuter sing. remains (e.g. <em>etad guru&#x1e63;u v&#x1e5b;tti&#x1e25;</em>, this is the custom among Gurus <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> ii, 206) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>etad</em> generally refers to what precedes, esp. when connected with <em>idam</em>, the latter then referring to what follows (e.g. <em>e&#x1e63;a vai prathama&#x1e25; kalpa&#x1e25;</em> <em>anukalpas tv aya&#x1e43; j&#x00f1;eya&#x1e25;</em>, this before-mentioned is the principal rule, but this following may be considered a secondary rule <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> iii, 147) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; it refers also to that which follows, esp. when connected with a relative clause (e.g. <em>e&#x1e63;a c&#x00e2;iva gurur dharmo yam pravak&#x1e63;y&#x0101;my aha&#x1e43; tava</em>, this is the important law, which I will proclaim to you <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (<em>&#x00e1;d</em>), ind. in this manner, thus, so, here, at this time, now (e.g. <em>n&#x00e1; v&#x0101;&#x0341; u et&#x00e1;n mriyase</em>, thou dost not die in this manner or by that <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> i, 162, 21) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> &amp;c. ; [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Zd">Zd.</a> <em>a&#x00ea;ta</em> ; Old Pers. <em>aita</em> ; Armen. <em>aid</em> ; Osk. <em>eiso</em>.]</dd>

[<em>enam</em>, <em>en&#x0101;m</em>, <em>enad</em>, &amp;c.], inst. sing. [<em>enena</em>, <em>enay&#x0101;</em>], gen. loc. du. [<em>enayos</em>, Ved. <em>enos</em>] </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the other cases are formed fr. the pronom. base <em>a</em>, under <em>idam</em>), he, she, it </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; this, that, (this pronoun is enclitic and cannot begin a sentence </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; it is generally used alone, so that <em>enam puru&#x1e63;am</em>, 'that man', would be very unusual if not incorrect. Grammarians assert that the substitution of <em>enam</em> &amp;c. for <em>imam</em> or <em>etam</em> &amp;c. takes place when something is referred to which has already been mentioned in a previous part of the sentence </dd>

           <dt>eva 1</dt>
           <dd><em>ev&#x00e1;</em> (in the Sa&#x1e43;hit&#x0101; also <em>ev&#x0101;&#x0341;</em>), ind. (&#x221a;<em>i</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#U&#x1e47;">U&#x1e47;.</a> i, 152 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; fr. pronom. base <em>e</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BRD">BRD.</a>, probably connected with 2. <em>&#x00e9;va</em>), so, just so, exactly so (in the sense of the later <em>evam</em>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#AV">AV.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; indeed, truly, really (often at the beginning of a verse in conjunction with other particles, as <em>id</em>, <em>hi</em>) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (in its most frequent use of strengthening the idea expressed by any word, <em>eva</em> must be variously rendered by such adverbs as) just, exactly, very, same, only, even, alone, merely, immediately on, still, already, &amp;c. (e.g. <em>tvam eva yant&#x0101; n&#x00e2;nyo'sti p&#x1e5b;thivy&#x0101;m</em>, thou alone art a charioteer, no other is on earth, i. e. thou art the best charioteer <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> iii, 2825 </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>t&#x0101;vat&#x012b;m eva r&#x0101;trim</em>, just so long as a night </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>evam</em> <em>eva</em> or <em>tath&#x00e2;iva</em>, exactly so, in this manner only </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in the same manner as above </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>ten&#x00e2;iva mantre&#x1e47;a</em>, with the same Mantra as above </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>apa&#x1e25; sp&#x1e5b;&#x1e63;&#x1e6d;v&#x00e2;iva</em>, by merely touching water </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>t&#x0101;n eva</em>, these very persons </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>na cir&#x0101;d eva</em>, in no long time at all </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>japyen&#x00e2;iva</em>, by sole repetition </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>abhuktv&#x00e2;iva</em>, even without having eaten </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>iti vadann eva</em>, at the very moment of saying so </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>sa j&#x012b;vann eva</em>, he while still living, &amp;c.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> &amp;c. <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (sometimes, esp. in connection with other adverbs, <em>eva</em> is a mere expletive without any exact meaning and not translatable, e.g. <em>tv eva</em>, <em>c&#x00e2;iva</em>, <em>eva ca</em>, &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; according to native authorities <em>eva</em> implies emphasis, affirmation, detraction, diminution, command, restrainment) ; [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Zd">Zd.</a> <em>aeva</em> ; Goth. <em>aiv</em> ; Old Germ. <em>eo</em>, <em>io</em> ; Mod. Germ. <em>je</em>.]</dd>

           <dt>&#x226b; evath&#x0101; </dt>
           <dd><em>ev&#x00e1;th&#x0101;</em> ind. so, just so, like <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> viii, 24, 15</dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; m. course, way (generally instr. pl.) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; the earth, world <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#VS">VS.</a> xv, 4 ; 5 [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mah&#x012b;dh">Mah&#x012b;dh.</a>] </dd>

           <dd>&#x2022; [<a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Gk">Gk.</a> ?, ? ; Lat. [232, 2] <em>aevu-m</em> ; Goth. <em>aivs</em> ; O&#x1e24;.G <em>&#x00ea;wa</em> and Angl. Sax. <em>&#x00ea;u</em>, <em>&#x00ea;o</em>, 'custom', 'law' ; Germ. <em>ehe</em>.]</dd>

           <dt>&#x22d9; evay&#x0101; </dt>
           <dd><em>&#x25cb;y&#x0101;&#x0341;</em> mfn. going quickly (said of Vish&#x1e47;u) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a> i, 156, 1 </dd>

           <dd><em>&#x25cb;y&#x0101;&#x0341;van</em> mf(<em>ar&#x012b;</em>)n. going quickly (said of Vish&#x1e47;u and the Maruts) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#RV">RV.</a></dd>

           <dt>evam </dt>
           <dd><em>ev&#x00e1;m</em> ind. (fr. pronom. base <em>e</em> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#BRD">BRD.</a> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; probably connected with 1. <em>ev&#x00e1;</em>), thus, in this way, in such a manner, such, (it is not found in the oldest hymns of the Veda, where its place is taken by 1. <em>ev&#x00e1;</em>, but occurs in later hymns ind in the Br&#x0101;hma&#x1e47;as, especially in connection with &#x221a;<em>vid</em>, 'to know', and its derivatives [e.g. <em>ya eva&#x1e43; veda</em>, he who knows so </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; cf. <em>eva&#x1e43;-v&#x00ed;d</em>, col. 3] </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; in classical Sansk&#x1e5b;it <em>evam</em> occurs very frequently, especially in connection with the roots <em>vac</em>, 'to speak', and <em>&#x015b;ru</em>, 'to hear', and refers to what precedes as well as to what follows [e.g. <em>evam uktv&#x0101;</em>, having so said <font color="#FF0000" font size=-2><a name="p232-3"></a>[Page 232, Column 3]</font> </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>evam ev&#x00e2;itat</em>, this is so </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>evam astu</em>, or <em>evam bhavatu</em>, be it so, I assent </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>asty evam</em>, it is so </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>yady evam</em>, if this be so </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; <em>kim evam</em>, how so? what is the meaning of it? what does this refer to? <em>m&#x00e2;ivam</em>, not so! <em>evam</em> - <em>yath&#x0101;</em> or <em>yath&#x0101;</em> - <em>evam</em>, so - as) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#Mn">Mn.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;ak">&#x015a;ak.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; (it is also often used like an adjective [e.g. <em>eva&#x1e43; te vacane rata&#x1e25;</em>, rejoicing in such words of thine ; where <em>evam</em> = <em>eva&#x1e43;-vidhe</em>]) <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#MBh">MBh.</a> <a href="worksAuthorsAbbrs.html#&#x015a;ak">&#x015a;ak.</a> &amp;c </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sometimes <em>evam</em> is merely an expletive </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; according to lexicographers <em>evam</em> may imply likeness (so) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; sameness of manner (thus) </dd>
           <dd>&#x2022; assent (yes, verily) </dd>
